❓:Given the function f(x)= frac{ln x}{x}, g(x)= frac{m}{x} + frac{1}{2} (minmathbb{R}). (I) When m=1, find the equation of the tangent line to the curve y=g(x) at x=1; (II) Determine the monotonic intervals of f(x) and compare the size of sqrt[2017]{2017} and sqrt[2016]{2016}.

🧠:[<think>Okay, so I have this problem here with two parts. Let me start with part (I). When m=1, I need to find the equation of the tangent line to the curve y=g(x) at x=1. Alright, so first, let me recall that the equation of a tangent line at a point x=a is given by y = g(a) + g’(a)(x - a). Since a is 1 here, I need to compute g(1) and g’(1).Given that m=1, g(x) = (1)/x + 1/2. So, let me compute g(1). Plugging in x=1, that's 1/1 + 1/2 = 1 + 0.5 = 1.5 or 3/2. So the y-coordinate when x=1 is 3/2.Now, the derivative g’(x). The derivative of 1/x is -1/x², and the derivative of 1/2 is 0. So g’(x) = -1/x². Then at x=1, g’(1) = -1/(1)² = -1. So the slope of the tangent line is -1.Putting that into the tangent line formula: y = g(1) + g’(1)(x - 1) = 3/2 + (-1)(x - 1). Let me simplify that. Distribute the -1: 3/2 - x + 1. Then combine the constants: 3/2 + 1 is 5/2. So the equation is y = -x + 5/2. Wait, is that right? Let me check again.Wait, 3/2 + (-1)(x - 1) is 3/2 -1*(x -1). So, expanding that: 3/2 -x +1. But 3/2 +1 is 5/2, so yes, y = -x +5/2. That seems correct.Let me just confirm. The tangent line at x=1 must pass through the point (1, 3/2) and have slope -1. If I plug x=1 into the equation y = -x +5/2, I get -1 +5/2 = 3/2, which matches. So that's correct. So part (I) done.Now moving on to part (II). Determine the monotonic intervals of f(x) = ln x / x. So to find where the function is increasing or decreasing, I need to compute its derivative and analyze the sign.First, find f’(x). Let's recall that f(x) = ln x / x. Using the quotient rule: derivative of numerator (1/x) times denominator minus numerator times derivative of denominator (1) all over denominator squared. So f’(x) = [ (1/x)*x - ln x *1 ] / x². Simplify numerator: 1 - ln x. So f’(x) = (1 - ln x)/x².Now, x² is always positive for x ≠ 0, but since f(x) is defined for x > 0 (since ln x is defined for x>0), we can ignore x=0. So the sign of f’(x) depends on the numerator: 1 - ln x.Set 1 - ln x = 0 to find critical points. Solving 1 - ln x =0 → ln x =1 → x=e. So critical point at x=e.Now, for intervals:- When x < e: ln x <1 → 1 - ln x >0 → f’(x) >0. So f is increasing on (0, e).- When x > e: ln x >1 → 1 - ln x <0 → f’(x) <0. So f is decreasing on (e, ∞).Therefore, the function f(x) increases on (0, e) and decreases on (e, ∞). So the monotonic intervals are (0, e] increasing and [e, ∞) decreasing. Wait, actually, since at x=e the derivative is zero, so it's a critical point. So the function is increasing up to x=e and then decreasing after that.So that's part (II) first half. The second part is to compare the size of 2017^(1/2017) and 2016^(1/2016). Hmm. So we need to compare these two numbers. Let me see.First, note that both are of the form n^(1/n). So perhaps the function f(n) = n^(1/n) is decreasing or increasing? If we can determine the monotonicity of f(n) for integer n, then we can compare 2016 and 2017.But f(n) is n^(1/n). Let me take the natural logarithm to make it easier: ln f(n) = (1/n) ln n. Let’s consider the function h(x) = (ln x)/x, which is exactly the function given in part (II). So h(n) = (ln n)/n. From part (II), we found that h(x) increases up to x=e and decreases after x=e. Since e is approximately 2.718, and 2016 and 2017 are both way larger than e, so h(x) is decreasing for x > e. Therefore, as n increases beyond e, h(n) decreases, meaning that (ln n)/n is decreasing, which implies that f(n) = e^{(ln n)/n} is also decreasing. Therefore, since 2017 >2016, h(2017) < h(2016), so (ln 2017)/2017 < (ln 2016)/2016. Therefore, exponentiating both sides, since the exponential function is increasing, we get 2017^(1/2017) < 2016^(1/2016). Hence, sqrt[2017]{2017} < sqrt[2016]{2016}.Wait, let me verify that again. If h(n) = (ln n)/n is decreasing for n >e, then larger n gives smaller h(n). Therefore, when we take the exponential, since h(n) is smaller, e^{h(n)} is smaller. So f(n) = e^{(ln n)/n} = n^(1/n) is decreasing for n >e. Thus, since 2017 >2016, f(2017) < f(2016). Therefore, 2017^(1/2017) < 2016^(1/2016). Therefore, the answer is that sqrt[2017]{2017} is less than sqrt[2016]{2016}.But just to make sure, let's perhaps test with smaller numbers. Let's take n=2 and n=3. So seems like after n=3, which is larger than e, the function starts decreasing. Wait, but n=3 is still, but h(3)=ln3/3≈1.0986/3≈0.366, h(4)=ln4/4≈1.386/4≈0.346, so decreasing. So h(3) is close to h(e). So h(n) increases up to n=3 (integer n), then decreases. So at integer points, the maximum is at n=3. Therefore, for integer n≥3, the function h(n) is decreasing. So for n≥3, h(n) is decreasing, so n^(1/n) is decreasing. Therefore, since 2017 >2016 ≥3, so 2017^(1/2017) <2016^(1/2016). Therefore, the conclusion holds.Therefore, part (II)'s second half is that sqrt[2017]{2017} is smaller than sqrt[2016]{2016}.Let me recap to make sure I didn't miss anything. For f(x)=lnx/x, we found it increases up to x=e and decreases after that. For x > e, ln x > 1, so 1 - ln x < 0, so f’(x) < 0: f is decreasing. Hence, f(x) is increasing on (0, e) and decreasing on (e, ∞). Now, comparing 2017^(1/2017) and 2016^(1/2016). Since 2016 and 2017 are both greater than e (~2.718), so x^(1/x) is decreasing for x > e. Therefore, since 2016 < 2017, and the function is decreasing, then 2016^(1/2016) > 2017^(1/2017). To find the equation of the tangent line at ( x = 1 ):1. Calculate ( g(1) ): [ g(1) = frac{1}{1} + frac{1}{2} = frac{3}{2} ]2. Compute the derivative ( g'(x) ): [ g'(x) = -frac{1}{x^2} ]3. 🔑:Solution: (I) When m=1, g(x)= frac{1}{x} + frac{1}{2}, thus g'(x)=-frac{1}{x^{2}}, therefore k=g'(1)=-1, g(1)=1+ frac{1}{2} = frac{3}{2}, therefore the equation of the tangent line to the curve y=g(x) at x=1 is y- frac{3}{2} =-(x-1), which simplifies to 2x+2y-5=0. (II) Since f(x)= frac{ln x}{x} is defined on (0,+infty), f'(x)= frac{1-ln x}{x^{2}}. Setting f'(x)=0, we find x=e. When 0 0, the function f(x) is increasing, when x > e, f'(x) 2016, thus frac{ln 2017}{2017} < frac{ln 2016}{2016}, i.e., ln 2017^{frac{1}{2017}} < ln 2016^{frac{1}{2016}}, therefore boxed{2017^{frac{1}{2017}} < 2016^{frac{1}{2016}}}.

❓:The sum of the binomial coefficients in the expansion of the binomial expression (sqrt[3]{x} - frac{1}{x})^n is 4096. Find the constant term.

🧠:[<think>Okay, let's see. I need to find the constant term in the expansion of (cube root of x minus 1 over x) raised to the nth power. But first, they tell me that the sum of the binomial coefficients is 4096. Hmm, I remember that the sum of the binomial coefficients can be found by plugging in 1 for all the variables. So, if I set x to 1, the expression becomes (1 - 1)^n, which is 0^n. Wait, that can't be right. If I substitute x = 1, the expression becomes (1 - 1)^n = 0^n, but the sum of the binomial coefficients is supposed to be 4096. Hmm, that's confusing.Wait, maybe I misunderstood. The binomial coefficients are the coefficients when you expand (a + b)^n, which are C(n,0), C(n,1), ..., C(n,n). The sum of these is 2^n. Oh! So, if the sum of the binomial coefficients is 4096, that means 2^n = 4096. Let me check that. 2^12 is 4096, right? Because 2^10 is 1024, 2^11 is 2048, 2^12 is 4096. So, n must be 12. Okay, that makes sense. So, n = 12. Got that down.Now, I need to find the constant term in the expansion of (∛x - 1/x)^12. Alright, let's recall how binomial expansion works. The general term in the expansion of (a + b)^n is C(n, k) * a^(n - k) * b^k. In this case, a is ∛x and b is -1/x. So, each term will be C(12, k) * (∛x)^(12 - k) * (-1/x)^k.Simplify that term. Let's write out the exponents. First, (∛x)^(12 - k) is the same as x^((12 - k)/3). Then, (-1/x)^k is (-1)^k * x^(-k). So, combining those, the exponent of x in each term is ((12 - k)/3) - k. Let me compute that: (12 - k)/3 - k = (12 - k - 3k)/3 = (12 - 4k)/3.We need the exponent of x to be zero for the constant term. So, set (12 - 4k)/3 = 0. Multiply both sides by 3: 12 - 4k = 0. Then, 4k = 12, so k = 3. So, the constant term occurs when k = 3.Now, let's compute that term. The coefficient is C(12, 3) * (-1)^3. First, C(12, 3) is 12 choose 3, which is 12! / (3! * 9!) = (12*11*10)/(3*2*1) = 220. Then, (-1)^3 is -1. So, the coefficient is 220 * (-1) = -220. Therefore, the constant term is -220. Wait, is that all? Let me check.Hold on, let me verify the exponent again. Let me re-derive the exponent. The term is (∛x)^(12 - k) * (-1/x)^k. So, ∛x is x^(1/3), so (x^(1/3))^(12 - k) is x^((12 - k)/3). Then, (-1/x)^k is (-1)^k * x^(-k). Multiply those together: x^((12 - k)/3) * x^(-k) = x^((12 - k)/3 - k). Combine the exponents: (12 - k)/3 - k = (12 - k - 3k)/3 = (12 - 4k)/3. Yes, that's correct. So, when (12 - 4k)/3 = 0, 12 - 4k = 0, so k = 3. That's right.So, the exponent is zero when k = 3, so the term is C(12, 3)*(-1)^3*x^0 = -220. So, the constant term is -220. Hmm. 🔑:Given that the sum of the binomial coefficients in the expansion of (sqrt[3]{x} - frac{1}{x})^n is equal to 2^n = 4096, we find that n = 12.Therefore, the general term of the expansion of (sqrt[3]{x} - frac{1}{x})^{12} is given by T_{r+1} = C_{12}^{r} cdot (-1)^r cdot x^{4 - frac{4r}{3}}.Setting 4 - frac{4r}{3} = 0, we solve for r and find r = 3. Thus, the constant term is T_4 = C_{12}^{3} cdot (-1)^3 = -220.Hence, the answer is boxed{-220}.This problem involves the application of the binomial theorem, properties of binomial coefficients, and the general term formula of a binomial expansion. It is considered a basic problem.

Let's denote (x = 2^a), so (4^a = (2^a)^2 = x^2). Then the equation becomes:(x^2 + 2^b + 5 = k^2).Rearranged, we get:(k^2 - x^2 = 2^b + 5).Which factors as:((k - x)(k + x) = 2^b + 5).Since (k) and (x) are positive integers (since (4^a) and the rest are positive), both (k - x) and (k + x) are positive integers, and (k - x < k + x). Also, since their product is (2^b + 5), which is a power of 2 plus 5, which is an odd number (since 2^b is even for (b geq 1), and 5 is odd; if (b = 0), 2^0=1, so 1 +5=6, which is even). Wait, so (2^b +5) is even when (b =0), and odd otherwise.But (k^2 - x^2 = (k - x)(k + x)). The product of two integers. Now, (k - x) and (k + x) have the same parity because (k) and (x) are both integers. If (k) and (x) are both even or both odd, then (k - x) and (k + x) are even. If one is even and the other is odd, their sum and difference would be odd. However, the right-hand side is either even (if (b=0)) or odd (if (b geq1)). So let's analyze both cases.Case 1: (b=0). Then (2^0 +5=1+5=6). So ((k -x)(k +x)=6). We need two factors of 6 such that (k -x < k +x) and both factors have the same parity. The factors of 6 are (1,6), (2,3). Now, check the parities:1. (1,6): 1 is odd, 6 is even → different parities. Not allowed.2. (2,3): 2 is even, 3 is odd → different parities. Not allowed.Therefore, no solutions when (b=0). Which matches our earlier result.Case 2: (b geq1). Then (2^b +5) is odd. Therefore, both (k -x) and (k +x) must be odd. Therefore, their product is odd. Since (k -x) and (k +x) are both odd, their sum (2k) is even, which it is, since (k) is an integer. So, moving on.So, given that (2^b +5) is odd, and we can factor it as two factors (d) and (e) such that (d leq e) and (d times e = 2^b +5), where both (d) and (e) are odd. Testing small values of (a) and (b): - For (a = 0): The expression becomes (1 + 2^b + 5 = 2^b + 6). Checking values of (b) from 0 to 6, none result in a perfect square. - For (a = 1): The expression becomes (4 + 2^b + 5 = 2^b + 9). Checking values of (b), we find (b = 4) gives (2^4 + 9 = 25), which is a perfect square. Thus, ((a, b) = (1, 4)) with (a + b = 5). - For (a = 2): The expression becomes (16 + 2^b + 5 = 2^b + 21). Checking values of (b), we find (b = 2) gives (2^2 + 21 = 25), which is a perfect square. Thus, ((a, b) = (2, 2)) with (a + b = 4). - For (a geq 3): Testing higher values of (a) and corresponding (b) shows no solutions as the resulting expressions do not form perfect squares.2. Algebraic approach and factorization: - We consider the equation (2^{2a} + 2^b + 5 = k^2) and factorize (2^b + 5) into pairs of factors differing by a power of two. This approach confirms the solutions found earlier.3. Verification of solutions: - The pairs ((a, b) = (1, 4)) and ((a, b) = (2, 2)) are the only solutions. Their sums (a + b) are 5 and 4, respectively.Summing these results, we get (5 + 4 = 9).[boxed{9}]]

🔑:To find the sum of all possible sums (a + b) where (a) and (b) are nonnegative integers such that (4^a + 2^b + 5) is a perfect square, we need to analyze the equation (4^a + 2^b + 5 = x^2) for integer solutions.1. Rewrite the equation: [ 4^a + 2^b + 5 = x^2 ] Since (4^a = 2^{2a}), we can rewrite the equation as: [ 2^{2a} + 2^b + 5 = x^2 ]2. Consider the case (a > 1) and (b > 2): If (a > 1) and (b > 2), we can analyze the equation modulo 8: [ 2^{2a} + 2^b + 5 equiv 0 pmod{8} ] Since (2^{2a} equiv 0 pmod{8}) for (a geq 1) and (2^b equiv 0 pmod{8}) for (b geq 3), we have: [ 0 + 0 + 5 equiv 5 pmod{8} ] This is not congruent to 0 modulo 8, so there are no solutions for (a > 1) and (b > 2).3. Consider specific values for (a) and (b): - Case (b = 2): [ 4^a + 4 + 5 = x^2 implies 4^a + 9 = x^2 ] This can be written as: [ 4^a = (x-3)(x+3) ] For (4^a) to be a product of two factors differing by 6, we need (x-3) and (x+3) to be powers of 2. The only solution is (a = 2) and (x = 5): [ 4^2 = (5-3)(5+3) implies 16 = 2 cdot 8 ] Thus, (a = 2) and (b = 2). - Case (b = 1): [ 4^a + 2 + 5 = x^2 implies 4^a + 7 = x^2 ] This can be written as: [ 4^a = (x-3)(x+3) ] There are no solutions in modulo 3, as (4^a equiv 1 pmod{3}) and (7 equiv 1 pmod{3}), but (x^2 equiv 1 pmod{3}) does not hold. - Case (a = 1): [ 4 + 2^b + 5 = x^2 implies 2^b + 9 = x^2 ] This can be written as: [ 2^b = (x-3)(x+3) ] For (2^b) to be a product of two factors differing by 6, we need (x-3) and (x+3) to be powers of 2. The only solution is (b = 4) and (x = 5): [ 2^4 = (5-3)(5+3) implies 16 = 2 cdot 8 ] Thus, (a = 1) and (b = 4). - Case (a = 0): [ 1 + 2^b + 5 = x^2 implies 2^b + 6 = x^2 ] If (b) is an odd number, there is no solution. If (b) is an even number, say (b = 2k), we can write: [ 2^b = (x-2^k)(x+2^k) ] Trying different values, we find no solutions. - Case (b = 0): [ 4^a + 1 + 5 = x^2 implies 4^a + 6 = x^2 ] This is similar to the case (a = 0) and has no solutions.4. Summarize the solutions: We have two solutions: [ (a, b) = (2, 2) quad text{and} quad (a, b) = (1, 4) ] Therefore, the possible sums (a + b) are: [ 2 + 2 = 4 quad text{and} quad 1 + 4 = 5 ]5. Sum of all possible sums: [ 4 + 5 = 9 ]The final answer is (boxed{9})

The problem says "one pair", so either is acceptable.Final AnswerOne such pair is boxed{(1, 18)}.</think>To solve the problem, we need to find positive integers (a) and (b) such that:1. (ab(a + b)) is not divisible by 7.2. ((a + b)^7 - a^7 - b^7) is divisible by (7^7).First, we note that for (ab(a + b)) to not be divisible by 7, none of (a), (b), or (a + b) can be divisible by 7. Next, we expand ((a + b)^7 - a^7 - b^7) using the binomial theorem and factor out common terms:[(a + b)^7 - a^7 - b^7 = 7ab(a + b)(a^2 + ab + b^2)^2]We need this expression to be divisible by (7^7). Since (ab(a + b)) is not divisible by 7, the term ((a^2 + ab + b^2)^2) must be divisible by (7^6). This implies (a^2 + ab + b^2) must be divisible by (7^3 = 343).We solve the congruence (a^2 + ab + b^2 equiv 0 pmod{343}). Starting with modulo 7, we find that (a equiv 2b pmod{7}) or (a equiv 4b pmod{7}). Using Hensel's lemma, we lift these solutions to modulo 343.After solving the congruences and lifting the solutions, we find that one pair of solutions is (a = 1) and (b = 18) (or vice versa). This pair satisfies both conditions:1. (ab(a + b) = 1 cdot 18 cdot 19 = 342), which is not divisible by 7.2. ((a + b)^7 - a^7 - b^7 = 19^7 - 1^7 - 18^7), which is divisible by (7^7) as shown by the factorization.Thus, one such pair is (boxed{(1, 18)}).]

🔑:We find that (a + b) 7 - a 7 - b 7 = 7ab(a + b)(a 2 + ab + b 2 ) 2 . So we must find a, b such that a 2 + ab + b 2 is divisible by 7 3 . At this point I found a = 18, b = 1 by trial and error. A more systematic argument turns on noticing that a 2 + ab + b 2 = (a 3 - b 3 )/(a - b), so we are looking for a, b with a 3 = b 3 (mod 7 3 ). We now remember that a φ(m) = 1 (mod m). But φ(7 3 ) = 2·3·49, so a 3 = 1 (mod 343) if a = n 98 . We find 2 98 = 18 (343), which gives the solution 18, 1. This approach does not give a flood of solutions. n 98 = 0, 1, 18, or 324. 🔑:2. A.Let b_{n}=a_{n}+1, thenb_{n+1}-1=frac{b_{n}^{2}-b_{n-1}}{b_{n-1}}=frac{b_{n}^{2}}{b_{n-1}}-1 .Therefore, b_{n}^{2}=b_{n+1} b_{n-1}. Hence b_{5}^{2}=b_{1} b_{9}=16.Thus, b_{5}=4 (discard -4, as b_{1} 、 b_{5} 、 b_{9} have the same sign).
